Getting started
# Welcome to the Omni docs!
Omni is the business intelligence platform that combines the consistency of a shared data model with the freedom of SQL. You don’t have to choose between a governed model and agile analysis. Focus on answering data questions, and Omni will build a data model as you go, allowing for reusability, governance, and performance optimization.
##
[​](https://docs.omni.co/#new-to-omni)
New to Omni?
Start here! Use our onboarding video collection to get up and running with Omni.

Getting started
# Omni REST APIs
Programmatically interact with your Omni instance with Omni’s REST APIs.
##
[​](https://docs.omni.co/api#base-url)
Base URL
The API base URL is the same as the URL you use to login to Omni. For example, if you log in using `https://blobsrus.omniapp.co`, your base URL will be `https://blobsrus.omniapp.co/api`. Only HTTPS calls are accepted.
You can interactively browse and test API endpoints using the [API Explorer](https://docs.omni.co/api/api-explorer), available at `/api-explorer` on your Omni instance.
##
[​](https://docs.omni.co/api#available-endpoints)
Available endpoints
Entity | Resource | Version
---|---|---
[AI](https://docs.omni.co/api/ai) | `/api/v1/ai` | v1
[Connections](https://docs.omni.co/api/connections) | `/api/v1/connections` | v1
[Schema refresh schedules](https://docs.omni.co/api/schema-refresh-schedules) | `/api/v1/connections/:connectionId/schedules` | v1
[Connection environments](https://docs.omni.co/api/connection-environments) | `/api/v1/connection-environments` | v1
[Content migration](https://docs.omni.co/api/content-migration) |  `/api/unstable/documents/:dashboardId/export`
`/api/unstable/documents/:dashboardId/import` | beta
[Content validator](https://docs.omni.co/api/content-validator) | `/api/v1/models/:modelId/content-validator` | v1
[Dashboard downloads](https://docs.omni.co/api/dashboard-downloads) | `/api/v1/dashboards/:dashboardId/download` | v1
[Documents](https://docs.omni.co/api/documents) | `/api/v1/documents` | v1
[Document model](https://docs.omni.co/api/documents) | `/api/unstable/documents/:documentId/update-model` | beta
[Document labels](https://docs.omni.co/api/document-labels) | `/api/v1/documents/:documentId/labels/:labelName` | v1
[Document favorites](https://docs.omni.co/api/document-favorites) | `/api/v1/documents/:documentId/favorite` | v1
[Document permissions](https://docs.omni.co/api/document-permissions) | `/api/v1/documents/:documentId/permissions` | v1
[Dashboard filters](https://docs.omni.co/api/dashboard-filters) | `/api/v1/dashboards/:dashboardId/filters` | v1
[Folders](https://docs.omni.co/api/folders) | `/api/v1/folders` | v1
[Folder permissions](https://docs.omni.co/api/folder-permissions) | `/api/v1/folders/:folderId/permissions` | v1
[Jobs](https://docs.omni.co/api/jobs) | `/api/v1/jobs/:jobId/status` | v1
[Labels](https://docs.omni.co/api/labels) | `/api/v1/labels` | v1
[Models](https://docs.omni.co/api/models) | `/api/v1/models` | v1
[Model git configuration](https://docs.omni.co/api/model-git-configuration) | `/api/v1/models/:modelId/git` | v1
[Model YAML](https://docs.omni.co/api/models) | `/api/v1/models/:modelId/yaml` | v1
[Model branches](https://docs.omni.co/api/model-branches) | `/api/v1/models/:modelId/branch/:branchName/merge` | v1
[Queries](https://docs.omni.co/api/queries) | `/api/v1/query/run` | v1
[Schedules](https://docs.omni.co/api/schedules) | `/api/v1/schedules` | v1
[Topics](https://docs.omni.co/api/topics) | `/api/v1/models/:modelId/topics` | v1
[Users](https://docs.omni.co/api/users) | `/scim/v2/users` | SCIM 2.0
[User attributes](https://docs.omni.co/api/user-attributes) | `/api/v1/user-attributes` | v1
[Uploads](https://docs.omni.co/api/uploads) | `/api/v1/uploads` | v1
[User groups](https://docs.omni.co/api/user-groups) | `/scim/v2/groups` | SCIM 2.0

Model data
# Modeling in Omni
  1. A schema model that mirrors the database
  2. A shared, virtualized data model for global business metrics and definitions
  3. A workbook model for ad hoc analysis that extends the core data models

As metrics are refined, they can be promoted from a workbook into your organization’s shared model, and, eventually into the database schema beneath Omni.
##
[​](https://docs.omni.co/modeling#core-philosophies)
Core philosophies
The Omni data model is composed of layers. The schema model reflects the raw database, with subsequent layers above. The shared model represents the universal, governed data model that each new workbook is based on. Finally the workbook model extends the schema model and shared model. This is a simple way to think about modeling in Omni: ![](https://mintcdn.com/omni-e7402367/6ikujnGo2ytdwGbR/images/docs/modeling/assets/images/1-model-layers-0e641a57d2cdb1e9508ad3ff813995a2.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=6ikujnGo2ytdwGbR&q=85&s=0a69cdd291ce44cc80a71f46c866eef7) Even **branches** in Omni act as another layer on the model, right between the **shared** and **workbook** models, created when you enter branch mode. When developing a data model in Omni, it’s often best to start by modeling in the workbook or in a branch. Joins and fields can then be promoted to the shared model for consumption by all workbooks.
##
[​](https://docs.omni.co/modeling#model-structure)
Model structure
See docs on [schema model](https://docs.omni.co/modeling/develop/model-generation) and [shared model](https://docs.omni.co/modeling/develop/model-generation#model-extension). If the schema looks out of sync with the database, simply refresh the schema in the UI.
##
[​](https://docs.omni.co/modeling#validation)
Validation
Omni models have strong validation. Errors in YAML syntax or property names are rejected without being saved. This will be softened over time and the UX will be improved, but be aware that invalid code may be rejected on save in the data model. Field typing is implicit in Omni based upon the dialect and functions applied. To change types, simply cast fields in SQL. When the schema model is updated, breakage can occur in layers above. The model IDE will provide pointers to broken field references to resolve any issues, for example when columns are deleted beneath Omni. ![](https://mintcdn.com/omni-e7402367/6ikujnGo2ytdwGbR/images/docs/modeling/assets/images/validation-error-91ebb768bd2db140130f73bd87068784.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=6ikujnGo2ytdwGbR&q=85&s=4e2dfffaad9beb75eb3a404f7b42550a)
Was this page helpful?
YesNo

Manage content
# Organizing content with folders & labels
As your team creates content, finding the right balance between access and findability becomes crucial. Omni’s content system allows you to efficiently manage your content with:
  * **Folders** , which provide a simple, hierarchical structure for organizing content and controlling access
  * **Labels** , which can enhance findability without the need for duplicating content across folders

By combining folders and labels, you can create an intuitive content organization system that supports your team’s collaboration by ensuring that the right content is always easy to find.
##
[​](https://docs.omni.co/content/organize#folders)
Folders
Using folders for content organization allows you to maintain structure and determine how users access content. For example, folders could allow you to organize content and access for:
  * Teams, such as **Operations** or **Finance**
  * Employee level, such as **Manager** or **Executive**
  * Projects
  * Clients

Folders can contain documents and subfolders.
###
[​](https://docs.omni.co/content/organize#creating-folders)
Creating folders
To create a folder, click **Add folder** in the **My documents** folder or your organization’s **Shared** hub. **Note** : Your [organization’s **Content organization** setting](https://docs.omni.co/administration/settings) determines if users can create content in the root of the shared space. Creating subfolders in folders is supported. The parent folder can contain up to seven levels of nesting, for example:
Copy
Ask AI
```
. Shared (root)               ## Parent folder
└── Folder 1
    └── Folder 2
        └── Folder 3
            └── Folder 4
                └── Folder 5
                    └── Folder 6
                        └── Folder 7   ## Nesting limit

```

###
[​](https://docs.omni.co/content/organize#moving-folders)
Moving folders
  1. To move a folder:
     * Open the folder and click the **Options menu (three dots)** next to the **Share** icon, or
     * On a page like the shared **Hub** or **My Documents** , click the **Options (three dots) menu** next to the folder: ![](https://mintcdn.com/omni-e7402367/rE0DLfCWKMXIHEkL/images/docs/finding-content/assets/images/folder-move-option-37bd04ed47ff847f601348166f7030ec.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=rE0DLfCWKMXIHEkL&q=85&s=2f8ad57f86c869f66b05ac07645a01db)
  2. Click **Move**.
  3. Select the folder to move to.
  4. Click **Save**.


###
[​](https://docs.omni.co/content/organize#accessing-and-sharing-folders)
Accessing and sharing folders
The contents of a folder - including any subfolders - will inherit the access role of the parent folder. Refer to the [Sharing content guide](https://docs.omni.co/share#inheriting-access-roles) for more information and examples.
###
[​](https://docs.omni.co/content/organize#deleting-folders)
Deleting folders
Folders can only be deleted if they’re empty. Who can delete a folder depends on their [content access role](https://docs.omni.co/share#content-access-permissions):
  * **Editors** can delete empty folders they created
  * **Managers** can delete any empty folder they have access to

To delete a folder, click the folder’s **Options** menu (three dots) and then **Delete**.
##
[​](https://docs.omni.co/content/organize#labels)
Labels
While folders are helpful for maintaining structure and access, a document can only be in one folder at a time. For example, a dashboard is relevant to multiple teams, each of which has their own folder. Where should the document be located? With labels, you could place the dashboard in a shared folder and add relevant labels, ensuring the right people can find the content. Labels allow you to organize your content in a way that doesn’t require duplication or sacrifice findability. Using labels, you can:
  * Organize content by subject area, such as **Marketing** or **Support**
  * Indicate the current working state of a document, such as **In progress**
  * Use [label settings](https://docs.omni.co/content/organize#label-options) to:
    * Curate **Home** page content for your organization
    * Mark important content as **Verified**


###
[​](https://docs.omni.co/content/organize#applying-labels)
Applying labels
To apply a label to a document or a folder, click the **Labels** icon to the right of the document/folder name: ![](https://mintcdn.com/omni-e7402367/rE0DLfCWKMXIHEkL/images/docs/finding-content/assets/images/document-label-icon-37cdf6fa1966650fabcdc06276d2547a.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=rE0DLfCWKMXIHEkL&q=85&s=c698839d6cfadb4dce976e3dd556efb7) **Note** : You must be in the published version of a document to apply labels.
###
[​](https://docs.omni.co/content/organize#managing-labels)
Managing labels
Labels are managed in the **Label settings** page, which can be accessed by:
  * Navigating to **Settings > Labels**, or
  * Clicking the **Labels** icon in a document or folder, then the **gear icon**

On the **Label settings** page, you can:
  * **Add a label** by clicking the **Add Label** button.
  * **Rename a label** by clicking the **options menu** (three dots) next to the label and selecting **Rename**.
  * **Delete a label** by clicking the **options menu** (three dots) next to the label and selecting **Delete**. **Note** : Labels can’t be deleted if they’re currently in use.

You can also [curate labels](https://docs.omni.co/content/organize#label-options) which will give them additional functionality.
###
[​](https://docs.omni.co/content/organize#label-options)
Label options
####
[​](https://docs.omni.co/content/organize#homepage)
Homepage
Adding the **Homepage** option allows you to select content to display on your users’ **Home** page, in the **For you** section. This can be useful for:
  * Providing helpful starting points for new users in your organization
  * Ensuring content relevant to all users is easily accessible


####
[​](https://docs.omni.co/content/organize#verified)
Verified
Adding the **Verified** option allows you to mark important content, such as dashboards that are monitored for correctness. This can be helpful for conveying to your users which content is actively maintained or has been vetted. **Verified** labels can only be applied by users with instance admin permissions.
* * *
To apply these options to a label, click the **options menu** (three dots) next to a label and select one or both. Instance admin permissions are required to specify label settings. ![](https://mintcdn.com/omni-e7402367/rE0DLfCWKMXIHEkL/images/docs/finding-content/assets/images/labels-special-tags-563bce085bfb8bb43848f09512f89185.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=rE0DLfCWKMXIHEkL&q=85&s=dfbfa952fa435fac0d0031ea483a73ac) When the tags are applied, the corresponding label will be highlighted to increase prominence. Labels with the **Verified** tag will be highlighted green with a checkmark, while those with the **Homepage** tag will have a **Home Page** badge: ![](https://mintcdn.com/omni-e7402367/rE0DLfCWKMXIHEkL/images/docs/finding-content/assets/images/labels-special-tags-highlighted-86289d3825906b2dc03b2f6a686df604.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=rE0DLfCWKMXIHEkL&q=85&s=639fad5aa2bd12fa25c3706701db2577)
Was this page helpful?
YesNo

Analyze data
# Uploading CSVs with data input tables
Sometimes you may want to utilize data in an analysis that isn’t in one of your [database connections](https://docs.omni.co/connect-data/setup), whether it’s for data enrichment or an initial exploration. Creating a data input table allows you to add data to Omni, whether by manually entering data or uploading a CSV or XLSX, without needing to touch your data pipelines.
##
[​](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/data-input-csvs#requirements)
Requirements
To add data input tables, you’ll need:
  * **Restricted Querier** , **Querier** , or **Connection Admin** permissions
  * **To enable the[Upload data ability](https://docs.omni.co/share#controlling-document-interactivity)**. This setting must be enabled for the [organization](https://docs.omni.co/administration/content-permissions) and, if a document is shared with others, also in the [document’s settings](https://docs.omni.co/share#controlling-document-interactivity).


We also recommend that you create a schema in your database where Omni can write the CSV files. See the [setup guide for your database](https://docs.omni.co/connect-data/setup) for more instructions on write backs.
##
[​](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/data-input-csvs#limitations)
Limitations
Currently, data input tables:
  * **Must be added in a workbook**
  * **Are limited to 500,000 rows**
  * **Can’t be used in joins unless the table is pushed to a database.** Setting the connection’s **Schema for table upload** property enables this functionality. Refer to the [setup guide for your database](https://docs.omni.co/connect-data/setup) for more information.


##
[​](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/data-input-csvs#adding-a-data-input-table-to-a-workbook)
Adding a data input table to a workbook
Data input tables can be added in the workbook of any document. In a workbook, navigate to **Edit > New blank table**. A new tab with a blank data input table will display. ![](https://mintcdn.com/omni-e7402367/h5qjF0QQ3U3_AvLH/images/analyze-explore/csvs/source-table-tab.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=h5qjF0QQ3U3_AvLH&q=85&s=dc9a6ee353ecdcdcbfaee710e0f72219) To get data into the table, you can manually enter it or upload a CSV or XLSX: Once there’s data in the table, click **Query CSV** to create a query using the data. The table will also become available in the field picker in other queries.
##
[​](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/data-input-csvs#querying-and-joining-data-input-tables)
Querying and joining data input tables
Data input tables can be queried like any other table, including using the field picker, [SQL editor](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/sql), or working with [calculations and formulas](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/calculations). ![](https://mintcdn.com/omni-e7402367/h5qjF0QQ3U3_AvLH/images/analyze-explore/csvs/new-source-query.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=h5qjF0QQ3U3_AvLH&q=85&s=1a2ad070c03395cc9cdd8b9d111ca7d7) **Note** : To make the data available outside of the workbook, you’ll need to [promote it to the shared model](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/data-input-csvs#modeling-and-promoting-data-input-tables). How you join data from a data input table to other data depends on whether table uploads are enabled for the database connection used by the workbook:
##
[​](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/data-input-csvs#modeling-and-promoting-data-input-tables)
Modeling and promoting data input tables
When a data input table is added to a workbook, a few things will happen in the [workbook model](https://docs.omni.co/modeling/develop/promotion#reviewing-and-promoting-workbook-changes). To make the changes available outside of the workbook, [they must be promoted to the shared model](https://docs.omni.co/modeling/develop/promotion).
  * **A[view](https://docs.omni.co/modeling/views) representing the data input table will be created**. These views can be identified by the presence of an `uploaded_table_name` parameter:
products.view
Copy
Ask AI
```
# Reference this view as products
uploaded_table_name: products.csv::1a3497f5-cba8-47c0-bab9-b2df84d1b141

```

  * **A[topic](https://docs.omni.co/modeling/topics) based on the view representing the data input table will be created if**:
    * **Create topic** was selected while uploading a CSV or XLSX, or
    * A Restricted Querier performed the upload

Views and topics created from data input tables can be modeled like any other view or topic. However, if the data input table hasn’t been pushed to the connection’s database, attempting to use the data input table in a join in the IDE will result in the following content validation error:
Copy
Ask AI
```
View "<view_name>" references an uploaded table. Uploaded tables cannot be used in joins.

```

If data from a data input table hasn’t been pushed to a database, only `XLOOKUP` can be used to perform joins to other tabs in a workbook. Refer to the [Querying & joining data](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/data-input-csvs#querying-and-joining-data-input-tables) section for more information and examples.
##
[​](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/data-input-csvs#updating-data-input-table-data)
Updating data input table data
When making updates to a data input table, keep the following in mind:
  * **Changes must be promoted to the shared model to be accessible outside the workbook**. This is necessary even if the table was previously promoted to the shared model.
  * **If table uploads (writebacks) are enabled for the connection** , Omni will create a new table in the database each time the table is saved. You can manage previous versions of the table in the [**Upload management** page](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/data-input-csvs#managing-previous-table-versions).

To update a data input table’s data:
  1. In a workbook, locate the table in a query tab.
  2. Click the options menu next to the table’s name, then **Edit Table** : ![](https://mintcdn.com/omni-e7402367/h5qjF0QQ3U3_AvLH/images/analyze-explore/csvs/edit-table-menu.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=h5qjF0QQ3U3_AvLH&q=85&s=1cd3f3c36638a0261852c2ce1b75ba01)
  3. The data input table will open in a new tab where you can edit the data as needed.
  4. Click **Save changes** when finished.

Upon a successful save, the updated table will immediately become available in the workbook. Omni will also log a new version of the table in the [**Upload management** page](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/data-input-csvs#managing-previous-table-versions).
##
[​](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/data-input-csvs#managing-previous-table-versions)
Managing previous table versions
Every time you [create](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/data-input-csvs#adding-a-data-input-table-to-a-workbook) or [update](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/data-input-csvs#updating-data-input-table-data) a data input table, Omni adds an entry in the **Upload management** page. Each item in the list represents a version of the table. Entries are sorted by the time they were created, beginning with the most recent. Navigate to **Settings > Uploads** to access this page: ![](https://mintcdn.com/omni-e7402367/h5qjF0QQ3U3_AvLH/images/analyze-explore/csvs/upload-management-page.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=h5qjF0QQ3U3_AvLH&q=85&s=4fcb85d299c985ef1d32a6ca8874cf82)
###
[​](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/data-input-csvs#querying-previous-table-versions)
Querying previous table versions
To create a query using a specific version of a table, click the **Explore** button next to the table version. This will open a new workbook that uses the specified version of the table. **Note** : If you promote the changes from an older version of the table, it will overwrite the data currently in the shared model.
###
[​](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/data-input-csvs#deleting-table-versions)
Deleting table versions
**Deleting a table version can’t be undone**. Before continuing, note that:
  * The version of the table will be permanently deleted from your Omni instance. If table uploads (writebacks) are enabled, the version of the table will also be deleted from the database.
  * Queries, views, and topics built on the version will result in an error after the deletion


The **Upload management** page can be used to delete previous versions of a data input table. **Note** : Table versions are listed in the order they were created, meaning that the most recent version of a table will be higher in the list.
  1. Navigate to **Settings > Uploads**.
  2. Locate the version you want to remove and click **Delete**.

After the deletion is complete, you’ll also need to:
  * Remove views and topics built on the version from the model
  * Update or remove queries using the version

Getting started
# Omni best practices
Best practices, tips, and tricks to keep your model clean and your environment intuitive to navigate for your entire organization.
This guide covers best practices, tips, and tricks to keep your model clean and your environment intuitive to navigate for your entire organization. We leaned on our team’s experience building across many customers, so we hope it can provide a helpful starting place as you build. Let us know if you have questions about anything not covered here, as we will continue to update and improve this guide!
##
[​](https://docs.omni.co/getting-started/best-practices#use-labels-to-organize-and-verify-content)
Use labels to organize and verify content
  * [Curate the homepage](https://docs.omni.co/content/organize#label-options) by setting labels to display on the “Homepage”
  * Signal to users which content should be trusted by [marking as verified](https://docs.omni.co/content/organize#label-options)
  * Have users [favorite](https://docs.omni.co/content/navigate#personal) content


##
[​](https://docs.omni.co/getting-started/best-practices#create-tailored-content-and-workflows-for-users)
Create tailored content and workflows for users
  * Build Dashboards for specific use cases + set of users (don’t try to do too much on a single dashboard!)


###
[​](https://docs.omni.co/getting-started/best-practices#dashboard-design)
Dashboard design
  * Simplify Axis Labels
  * Create a unified color scheme
  * KPI tiles or headers go a long way. Try the built in [KPI](https://docs.omni.co/visualize-present/visualizations/types/markdown) vis or customize with [markdown](https://docs.omni.co/showcase/visualizations/gradient-card).
  * Take advantage of markdown visualizations to create customized dashboards including [nice headers](https://docs.omni.co/showcase/visualizations/gradient-card) or [data readouts](https://docs.omni.co/showcase/visualizations/data-readout) or something [custom](https://docs.omni.co/showcase/visualizations/image-grid)!
  * Reach out to Omni for additional ideas or inspiration


###
[​](https://docs.omni.co/getting-started/best-practices#additional-workflows)
Additional workflows
  * Define drill fields on measures to allow users to “drill deeper” into data. We recommend defining [`default_drill_fields`](https://docs.omni.co/modeling/views/parameters/default-drill-fields) for each view so that you won’t need to specify for each measure.
  * Utilize [links](https://docs.omni.co/modeling/dimensions/parameters/links) and [embedding](https://docs.omni.co/embed) to get data in front of users where they need it. Links can be really helpful to create workflows between dashboards or jump out to external applications. Embedding options allow you to bring other applications into Omni dashboards or embed Omni into external applications to bring data in front of users where they need it most.
  * Don’t rely on users navigating to a dashboard, set up a [scheduled delivery](https://docs.omni.co/share) to get data in front of users regularly.


##
[​](https://docs.omni.co/getting-started/best-practices#encourage-self-service)
Encourage self-service
Topics are a mechanism for creating reusable environments and are especially valuable to encourage self-service. Best practices when creating topics:
  * Consider what sorts of questions the users you are onboarding are likely to have, and whether you have an appropriate topic set up for them to do so. Starting with the core datasets each team cares about and the most common questions you answer for them will help you prepare the environment.
  * We typically recommend several smaller topics rather than one big topic. This can help for both usability and performance.
  * For most topics, you’ll want to have your base table be the one that’s the most granular, then join out with many-to-one or one-to-one joins.
  * Avoid many-to-many joins if possible. Instead consider creating multiple topics or pre-aggregating one side of the join.
  * Don’t overpopulate the shared model. Again, start by defining the basics you know will be used and add additional fields and logic as requests come in over time. Leave one-off definitions in workbooks if they won’t be re-used in other workbooks.
  * Organize your topics to help users understand where to go and how to find what they need. `group_label` on the [field](https://docs.omni.co/modeling/dimensions/parameters/group-label) and [topic](https://docs.omni.co/modeling/topics/parameters/group-label) level are tools to help you organize.
  * Translate database columns/tables to language familiar to users using [`label`](https://docs.omni.co/modeling/dimensions/parameters/label) and [`description`](https://docs.omni.co/modeling/dimensions/parameters/description).
  * [`hidden`](https://docs.omni.co/modeling/dimensions/parameters/hidden), [`ignored`](https://docs.omni.co/modeling/dimensions/parameters/ignored), and [`field`](https://docs.omni.co/modeling/topics/parameters/fields) parameters can be used to limit the fields and not overwhelm users.
  * Set up [`default_filters`](https://docs.omni.co/modeling/topics/parameters/default-filters) or [`always_where_sql`](https://docs.omni.co/modeling/topics/parameters/always-where-sql) to ensure users have the correct defaults applied to their analyses / avoid querying excessive volumes of data on large tables.


##
[​](https://docs.omni.co/getting-started/best-practices#general-development)
General development
  * Promote common or frequently used logic to the shared model. The general rule of thumb for promotion is whenever you’re utilizing the logic in several workbooks and that logic is non-trivial, that’s a good signal to promote to the shared model. On the flip side, keep logic that is specific to a single dashboard in the workbook rather than polluting the shared model.
  * Utilize the semantic model for repeatable patterns and self-service exploration. For one-off cases or patterns involving subqueries and window functions, it might be quickest and easiest to write a query in SQL. Otherwise, we recommend breaking down common SQL queries and building reusable patterns into the model. While it might take extra time upfront, the payoff in maintenance and reusability over time can be huge.
  * Utilize Omni field references (e.g. `${field_name}`) rather than the raw table name whenever possible. This helps simplify maintenance by only needing to update the field in one place, should the underlying column name or logic change.
  * Utilize [filtered measures](https://docs.omni.co/modeling/filters) when possible rather than writing a case when directly in the SQL of a measure. This allows Omni to pass through filters on drill fields.
  * Use [`ignored_schemas`](https://docs.omni.co/modeling/models/ignored-schemas), [`included_schemas`](https://docs.omni.co/modeling/models/ignored-schemas), and [`ignored_views`](https://docs.omni.co/modeling/models/ignored-views) to define relevant schemas and tables in Omni.
  * Push heavy queries into the database (both long-running queries and queries performing large transformations) using a transformation or orchestration tool like [DBT](https://www.getdbt.com).
  * Set up the [dbt integration](https://omni.co/blog/three-ways-to-use-our-dbt-integration) if you’re currently using dbt. This will allow you to pull through descriptions for views and fields you may already be setting, as well as table config information into Omni that can be viewed in the IDE. You can also push back net new dbt models from the workbook for a bi-directional workflow.


##
[​](https://docs.omni.co/getting-started/best-practices#administration)
Administration
  * Use the principle of least privilege for your Omni permission structure. When a user has a different level of permissions compared to the connection default, the more permissive level wins. Thus, if concerned about security it is best to leave the connection default at a low level of permissions such as viewer or restricted querier and give individuals or groups increased levels of access.
  * Leverage user groups to make permissioning and implementation of user attributes easier to manage.
  * Make it easy to get help: if you don’t already have one, we highly recommend having an internal Slack/Teams channel for people to ask analytics-related questions (and see each others’ questions), or at least a clear process of where and how to get help around data.
  * A little documentation goes a long way: pulling together a quick description of what data sources are available in Omni and what the topics are can be really helpful. We’ve seen this done successfully in anything from Notion/Confluence to Google Docs.


##
[​](https://docs.omni.co/getting-started/best-practices#content-organization-and-permissions)
Content Organization and Permissions
These are suggestions on possible implementations of content permissioning that may suit your organization. There are many possible combinations of how to apply permissions to your organization’s content. This table provides a quick comparison of best practices for content sharing within closed, open with restrictions, and very open systems across different aspects of file organization, permissions, and sharing.
| Closed System | Open System with Restrictions | Very Open System
---|---|---|---
**File Naming** | Utilize clear, descriptive names | Maintain clear and organized names | Prioritize descriptive, standardized names
**Content Organization** |  **Hub:** Organization-wide sharing |  **Hub:** Open visibility, restrictions on modification |  **Hub:** Maximum transparency, open access
|  **Shared with me:** Directly shared content |  **Shared with me:** Restricted access to direct shares |  **Shared with me:** Open access to shared content
**Content Permissions** |  **Roles:** most users and content in this system are assigned Viewer roles. Editor and Manager roles are assigned with caution. |  **Roles:** most users and content in this system are assigned Viewer roles. Editor roles are assigned more liberally. Manager roles are still assigned to users and content with caution. |  **Roles:** users in this system can have any role with little to no caution.
|  **AccessBoost:** Use with extreme caution. Content and users that have this enabled will be able to access all data on dashboards irrespective of their assigned roles as a user or the permission role on the dashboard. |  **AccessBoost:** Cautious use |  **AccessBoost:** can be used
**Setting Permissions for Users or Groups** | Explicitly opted-in users/groups | Permissions based on project teams | Promote a culture of collaboration
**Default Permissions** | Defaults to Viewer at the organization level | Defaults to Editor at the organization level | Defaults to Editor or Manager at the organization level
| Audit and update content permissions regularly |  |
Periodic training on permission management | Loose content permission regulations |  |
**Best Practices** | Cautiously selected opt-ins | Moderate restrictions | Very open with maximum transparency

AI
# IDE plugins
Extend your IDE with Omni analytics skills for building models, running queries, managing content, and more.
Omni’s IDE plugins bring analytics capabilities directly into your development environment. They are open-source plugins that let you explore models, run queries, build dashboards, and manage your Omni instance — all without leaving your IDE. Both plugins use Omni’s REST API and share a common set of skills that activate automatically based on your request.
IDE plugins are different from the [MCP Server](https://docs.omni.co/ai/mcp). The MCP Server enables natural language querying of your data, while IDE plugins provide a broader set of skills for model building, content management, administration, and more.
##
[​](https://docs.omni.co/ai/ide-plugins#available-plugins)
Available plugins
## [Claude Code Plugin for the command-line AI coding assistant ](https://github.com/exploreomni/omni-claude-skills)## [Cursor Plugin for the AI-powered code editor ](https://github.com/exploreomni/omni-cursor-plugin)
##
[​](https://docs.omni.co/ai/ide-plugins#what-you-can-do)
What you can do
  * Explore and inspect semantic models, topics, views, and fields
  * Run queries against Omni’s semantic layer
  * Create and edit model definitions in YAML
  * Find, browse, and manage dashboards and workbooks
  * Build and update dashboards programmatically
  * Optimize models for [Blobby](https://docs.omni.co/ai/chat) (Omni’s AI assistant)
  * Manage users, groups, permissions, and schedules


##
[​](https://docs.omni.co/ai/ide-plugins#authentication)
Authentication
Both plugins authenticate using environment variables:
Copy
Ask AI
```
export OMNI_BASE_URL="https://yourorg.omniapp.co"
export OMNI_API_KEY="your-api-key"

```

Create an API key in **Settings > API Keys** (Organization Admin) or **User Profile > Manage Account > Generate Token** (personal access token). See the [API authentication guide](https://docs.omni.co/api/authentication) for details.
##
[​](https://docs.omni.co/ai/ide-plugins#updating)
Updating
To ensure IDE plugins are up-to-date, enable automatic updates, update them manually from your IDE, or reinstall the plugin. Refer to the documentation for your IDE for information about enabling automatic updates.

Analyze data
# Workbook inspector
The workbook inspector provides a detailed view of your query and visualization configuration, making it easy to understand how your queries are structured and copy them to your model for reuse.
The inspector is useful for:
  * **Understanding query structure** : See exactly how Omni is interpreting your point-and-click query building
  * **Creating sample queries** : Quickly copy queries from workbooks to topic files for AI context and example queries
  * **Debugging queries** : Compare the query configuration to the generated SQL to troubleshoot issues
  * **Learning YAML syntax** : See how your UI actions translate to YAML configuration for modeling


##
[​](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/workbook-inspector#opening-the-inspector)
Opening the inspector
There are two ways to open the inspector in a workbook:
  * Click **View > Inspector**
  * Click the

The inspector will open as a side panel showing the configuration for the current query: ![](https://mintcdn.com/omni-e7402367/9IuE_N3sQTar3tg8/analyze-explore/images/workbook-inspector-panel.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=9IuE_N3sQTar3tg8&q=85&s=732ae3d4f9d2792ea6f0d46f9709287e)
##
[​](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/workbook-inspector#inspector-sections)
Inspector sections
The inspector contains a few sections:
  * [**Dialect SQL**](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/workbook-inspector#dialect-sql) - **Requires Querier or higher permissions**. Displays the query written in the SQL dialect of the database backing the connection.
  * [**Query structure**](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/workbook-inspector#query-structure) - The query represented in Omni’s query language
  * [**Vis config**](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/workbook-inspector#visualization-configuration-vis-config) - The configuration of the visualization associated with the query, if any


###
[​](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/workbook-inspector#dialect-sql)
Dialect SQL
**Querier** permissions or higher are required to view dialect SQL.
The **Dialect SQL** section in the inspector displays the query written in the same SQL dialect as the database backing the connection. All field references and Omni functions will be translated to the flavor of SQL used by your database. In fact, you could copy this SQL query and run it in another IDE pointed at the database. ![](https://mintcdn.com/omni-e7402367/9IuE_N3sQTar3tg8/analyze-explore/images/workbook-inspector-dialect-sql.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=9IuE_N3sQTar3tg8&q=85&s=fc4f9be6194f83ef4b2fc84fd481ceb7)
###
[​](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/workbook-inspector#query-structure)
Query structure
The **Query structure** section in the inspector displays the complete query configuration: ![](https://mintcdn.com/omni-e7402367/9IuE_N3sQTar3tg8/analyze-explore/images/workbook-inspector-query-structure.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=9IuE_N3sQTar3tg8&q=85&s=e10eab360eea7c73dd9a51943e8abb32) This can include:
  * Fields selected in the query
  * Base view or topic
  * Filters applied to the query
  * Sorts and limits
  * Calculations
  * Pivots
  * Period-over-period settings

You can toggle between JSON and YAML formats using the format selector at the top of the section.
###
[​](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/workbook-inspector#visualization-configuration-vis-config)
Visualization configuration (vis config)
While the Vis Config section will be present even when viewing the results table, it may not be populated. This section of the inspector will only populate when viewing a visualization.
The **Vis Config** section in the inspector displays the visualization settings for the current chart: ![](https://mintcdn.com/omni-e7402367/9IuE_N3sQTar3tg8/analyze-explore/images/workbook-inspector-vis-config.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=9IuE_N3sQTar3tg8&q=85&s=255db8d05b8389c67e55d9be9de41d61) This includes:
  * Chart type
  * Color configuration
  * Axis settings
  * Series configuration
  * Other visualization-specific settings

You can toggle between JSON and YAML formats using the format selector at the top of the section.
##
[​](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/workbook-inspector#copying-configuration)
Copying configuration
Each section in the inspector includes a copy button that allows you to copy the configuration to your clipboard:
  * **Query structure copy button** : Copies just the query configuration
  * **Visualization config copy button** : Copies just the visualization configuration
  * **Copy query and visualization YAML button** (in inspector header): Copies both the query and visualization configuration in the [sample query format](https://docs.omni.co/modeling/topics/parameters/sample-queries) ready to paste into a topic file: ![](https://mintcdn.com/omni-e7402367/9IuE_N3sQTar3tg8/analyze-explore/images/workbook-inspector-copy-all.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=9IuE_N3sQTar3tg8&q=85&s=d9bcfc368b0ab8701c3a4a452a8e7a7b)


###
[​](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/workbook-inspector#copying-queries-to-topics-as-sample-queries)
Copying queries to topics as sample queries
The YAML format in the inspector matches the structure used in topic sample queries. To add a query as a sample query to a topic:
1
[](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/workbook-inspector)
Build your query in a workbook.
2
[](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/workbook-inspector)
Open the inspector and click **Copy query and visualization YAML** in the inspector header.
3
[](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/workbook-inspector)
Open the model IDE and navigate to your topic file.
4
[](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/workbook-inspector)
Paste the copied YAML into the `sample_queries` section of your topic file.
5
[](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/workbook-inspector)
Add a query name and any additional parameters like `description`, `prompt`, or `ai_context`.
##
[​](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/workbook-inspector#next-steps)
Next steps
  * Learn more about [sample queries in topics](https://docs.omni.co/modeling/topics/parameters/sample-queries)
  * Read about [building queries in workbooks](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/querying)
  * Explore the [model IDE](https://docs.omni.co/modeling/develop/guides/model-ide)


Was this page helpful?

Getting started
# Keyboard shortcuts
A compiled list of shortcuts throughout the app.
##
[​](https://docs.omni.co/getting-started/keyboard-shortcuts#global-shortcuts)
Global shortcuts
These shortcuts can be used anywhere in the Omni app.
Action | Mac | Windows
---|---|---
Open/close application search |  `command` + `/` |  `control` + `/`
##
[​](https://docs.omni.co/getting-started/keyboard-shortcuts#workbook-shortcuts)
Workbook shortcuts
These shortcuts apply in [workbooks](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore).
Action | Mac | Windows
---|---|---
New workbook tab |  `option` + `T` |  `alt` + `T`
Save workbook |  `command` + `S` |  `control` + `S`
Edit workbook (transition from View) |  `command` + `E` |  `control` + `E`
Toggle between results table / chart |  `option` + `1` |  `alt` + `1`
Toggle filters open / closed |  `option` + `2` |  `alt` + `2`
Toggle SQL block open / closed |  `option` + `3` |  `alt` + `3`
Toggle field picker open / closed |  `option` + `4` |  `alt` + `4`
Toggle options config open / closed |  `option` + `5` |  `alt` + `5`
Toggle [inspector panel](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/workbook-inspector) open / closed |  `option` + `9` |  `alt` + `9`
Toggle chart to full screen mode |  `option` + `.` |  `alt` + `.`
Toggle [AI Query helper](https://docs.omni.co/ai/queries) |  `option` + `command` + `8` |  `alt` + `control` + `8`
Run query |  `command` + `Return` |  `control` + `Enter`
Run query w/o cache |  `shift` + `command` + `Return` |  `shift` + `control` + `Enter`
Clear query |  `command` + `K` |  `control` + `K`
Clear field from query |  `shift` + `command` + `K` |  `shift` + `control` + `K`
Clear filters from query |  `option` + `command` + `K` |  `alt` + `control` + `K`
Clear query and switch model |  `shift` + `option` + `command` + `K` |  `shift` + `alt` + `control` + `K`
Focus field search |  `option` + `command` + `F` |  `alt` + `control` + `F`
Duplicate tab |  `command` + `D` |  `control` + `D`
Next tab |  `command` + `option` + `down` |  `control` + `alt` + `down`
Previous tab |  `command` + `option` + `up` |  `control` + `alt` + `up`
First tab |  `command` + `option` + `[` |  `control` + `alt` + `[`
Last tab |  `command` + `option` + `]` |  `control` + `alt` + `]`
Rename current tab |  `option` + `command` + `R` |  `alt` + `control` + `R`
##
[​](https://docs.omni.co/getting-started/keyboard-shortcuts#spreadsheet-tabs-shortcuts)
Spreadsheet tabs shortcuts
These shortcuts apply when working with [spreadsheet tabs](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/spreadsheet-tabs) in workbooks.
Action | Mac | Windows
---|---|---
Delete row or column |  `command` + `-` |  `control` + `-`
Insert row or column |  `command` + `+` |  `control` + `+`
Bold |  `command` + `B` |  `control` + `B`
Italic |  `command` + `I` |  `control` + `I`
Underline |  `command` + `U` |  `control` + `U`
Format as percentage |  `control` + `shift` + `5` |  `control` + `shift` + `5`
Cycle formula reference | `F4` | `F4`
##
[​](https://docs.omni.co/getting-started/keyboard-shortcuts#sql-editor-autocomplete-shortcuts)
SQL editor autocomplete shortcuts
These shortcuts apply when working in the [SQL editor](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/sql) in a workbook.
Action | Mac | Windows
---|---|---
Trigger autocomplete |  `control` + `space` |  `control` + `space`
Accept suggestion | `tab` | `tab`
Accept suggestion or insert newline | `return` | `Enter`
Close autocomplete popup | `esc` | `esc`
##
[​](https://docs.omni.co/getting-started/keyboard-shortcuts#dashboard-shortcuts)
Dashboard shortcuts
These shortcuts apply when viewing or editing a [dashboard](https://docs.omni.co/visualize-present/dashboards).
Action | Mac | Windows
---|---|---
Undo layout change |  `command` + `Z` |  `control` + `Z`
Redo layout change |  `shift` + `command` + `Z` |  `shift` + `control` + `Z`
Reset dashboard filters |  `command` + `K` |  `control` + `K`
Refresh dashboard |  `command` + `Return` |  `control` + `Enter`
Refresh dashboard without cache |  `shift` + `command` + `Return` |  `shift` + `control` + `Enter`
##
[​](https://docs.omni.co/getting-started/keyboard-shortcuts#table-shortcuts)
Table shortcuts
These shortcuts apply when interacting with tables in [workbooks](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/querying#interacting-with-tables) and [dashboard tiles](https://docs.omni.co/visualize-present/dashboards/charts#interacting-with-table-tiles). All gestures require the visualization to be in table view.
###
[​](https://docs.omni.co/getting-started/keyboard-shortcuts#selection)
Selection
Action | Mac | Windows
---|---|---
Select all cells |  `command` + `A` |  `control` + `A`
Copy selected cells |  `command` + `C` |  `control` + `C`
Clear selection (keyboard) | `escape` | `escape`
Move focused cell |  `arrow` keys |  `arrow` keys
Extend selection from anchor |  `shift` + `arrow` keys |  `shift` + `arrow` keys
Select a cell | `click` | `click`
Select range from anchor to cell |  `shift` + `click` |  `shift` + `click`
Add or remove cell from selection |  `command` + `click` |  `control` + `click`
Select a rectangular region |  `click` and drag |  `click` and drag
Select entire row |  `click` row number |  `click` row number
Extend selection through row |  `shift` + `click` row number |  `shift` + `click` row number
Add or remove row from selection |  `command` + `click` row number |  `control` + `click` row number
Select entire column |  `click` column header |  `click` column header
Extend selection through column |  `shift` + `click` column header |  `shift` + `click` column header
Add or remove column from selection |  `command` + `click` column header |  `control` + `click` column header
Clear selection (mouse) |  `click` outside table |  `click` outside table
When all cells are selected with `command`/`control` + `A`, column headers are included when copying.
###
[​](https://docs.omni.co/getting-started/keyboard-shortcuts#editing-and-interaction-workbooks-only)
Editing and interaction (workbooks only)
These shortcuts are only available in workbook tables. Dashboard tables are read-only.
Action | Mac | Windows
---|---|---
Edit calculation cell or expand cell | `enter` | `enter`
Edit a calculation cell | `double-click` | `double-click`
Open context menu | `right-click` | `right-click`
Reorder columns | Drag column header | Drag column header
Column reordering is not available in pivot tables.
###
[​](https://docs.omni.co/getting-started/keyboard-shortcuts#calculation-editing-workbooks-only)
Calculation editing (workbooks only)
These shortcuts apply when editing a [calculation](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/spreadsheet-tabs) in a workbook table.
Action | Mac | Windows
---|---|---
Save calculation | `enter` | `enter`
Cancel and exit editor | `escape` | `escape`
Insert cell range reference |  `shift` + `click` a cell |  `shift` + `click` a cell
##
[​](https://docs.omni.co/getting-started/keyboard-shortcuts#markdown-editor-shortcuts)
Markdown editor shortcuts
These shortcuts are available when editing [text tiles](https://docs.omni.co/visualize-present/dashboards/text-markdown) in a dashboard.
Action | Mac | Windows
---|---|---
Bold |  `command` + `B` |  `control` + `B`
Italic |  `command` + `I` |  `control` + `I`
Blockquote |  `shift` + `command` + `.` |  `shift` + `control` + `.`
Ordered list |  `shift` + `command` + `7` |  `shift` + `control` + `7`
Unordered list |  `shift` + `command` + `8` |  `shift` + `control` + `8`
##
[​](https://docs.omni.co/getting-started/keyboard-shortcuts#model-ide-shortcuts)
Model IDE shortcuts
These shortcuts apply when viewing or editing files in the [model IDE](https://docs.omni.co/modeling).
Action | Mac | Windows
---|---|---
Save file |  `command` + `S` |  `control` + `S`
Find / search |  `option` + `command` + `F` |  `alt` + `control` + `F`
Toggle file list open / closed |  `option` + `1` |  `alt` + `1`
Toggle model validation list open / closed |  `option` + `9` |  `alt` + `9`
Fold all sections in a file |  `command` + `K`, `command` + `0` |  `control` + `K`, `control` + `0`
Unfold all sections in a file |  `command` + `K`, `command` + `J` |  `control` + `K`, `control` + `J`

Analyze data
# Formatting & analyzing data with spreadsheet tabs
Omni’s spreadsheet tabs bring the power of traditional Excel spreadsheets into your existing reporting and analysis workflows, with the added benefit of always-on, live data.
Spreadsheet tabs are ideal for:
  * Creating richly formatted tables such as financial statements, invoices, or planning sheets
  * Performing ad hoc or exploratory analysis

![](https://mintcdn.com/omni-e7402367/pDLnBWL9E88CrUiD/images/docs/querying-and-sql/workbook/assets/images/spreadsheet-intro-1909a4dbf24bd53a7dcbbc4d12aa3158.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=pDLnBWL9E88CrUiD&q=85&s=021c74984776c82b7c1a24b49e6476e2) Because these spreadsheets are directly connected to your database via Omni queries, you no longer need to export or manually refresh data. You can build and maintain familiar spreadsheet workflows - such as reporting templates or budget trackers - confident that your data is accurate, current, and easy to work with.
##
[​](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/spreadsheet-tabs#how-it-works)
How it works
Spreadsheets are enabled by default, but **Organization Admins** can disable (or re-enable) them in the [Organization settings](https://docs.omni.co/administration/settings) with the **Create spreadsheets** setting.You can enable and disable spreadsheet tabs for individual documents by navigating to **File > Document settings > Abilities** in a saved document.
Spreadsheets are a type of tab that, when enabled, can be added to Omni workbooks. Other queries in the workbook can be connected to the spreadsheet and used as a data source. When queries are connected to a spreadsheet tab, a new sheet will be added inside the spreadsheet tab. You can then reference the data in the sheet like you normally would in Excel. Sheets that correspond to a workbook query will automatically update when the query changes. For example, if a new column is added to a query, the sheet associated with the query will be updated to include the new column.
###
[​](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/spreadsheet-tabs#limitations)
Limitations
The most important limitation relates to data usability outside of a spreadsheet tab. **Data in spreadsheets can’t be used in other queries or promoted to a shared model.** While you can work with query data by [connecting it to a spreadsheet tab](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/spreadsheet-tabs#connecting-workbook-queries), data created in the spreadsheet - for example, by manual entry or through the use of [formulas](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/spreadsheet-tabs#creating-formulas) - can’t be used elsewhere.
####
[​](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/spreadsheet-tabs#excel-differences)
Excel differences
  * **Some formulas may differ slightly from Excel**. Omni expects the majority of formulas to be the same, but we recommend using the [in-sheet formula builder](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/spreadsheet-tabs#creating-formulas) to verify the correct syntax.
  * **Changes in spreadsheet tabs aren’t autosaved.** You’ll need to [manually save your work](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/spreadsheet-tabs#saving-your-work) to ensure changes are persisted.
  * **Hotkeys aren’t an exact match**
  * **References may not reflect structural changes the same way as Excel.** Refer to the [Handling query changes](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/spreadsheet-tabs#handling-query-changes) section for more information and examples.
  * **Creating pivot tables isn’t supported**. If you need to create pivot tables, create a [“regular”](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore) or [SQL query tab](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/sql) to use Omni’s native [pivot](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/querying#pivoting) functionality. **Note** : You can connect queries containing pivots to spreadsheets as a data source.
  * **Creating in-sheet charts isn’t supported**. If you need to create a visualization, create a [“regular”](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore) or [SQL query tab](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/sql) to use Omni’s native [chart](https://docs.omni.co/visualize-present/visualizations/types) functionality.


##
[​](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/spreadsheet-tabs#adding-spreadsheets-to-workbooks)
Adding spreadsheets to workbooks
When spreadsheet tabs are enabled, you’ll see a **Spreadsheet** option when you create a new workbook or query tab. Click this option to add a **Sheet** tab to the workbook. The tab will display a blank sheet similar to what you’d see in an Excel workbook. At this point, you can [connect other workbook queries to the spreadsheet](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/spreadsheet-tabs#connecting-workbook-queries) to interact with your data.
##
[​](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/spreadsheet-tabs#adding-data-to-spreadsheets)
Adding data to spreadsheets
You can add data to spreadsheets by:
  * [**Connecting workbook queries**](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/spreadsheet-tabs#connecting-workbook-queries) - **Recommended**. Creates additional sheets containing query data in the spreadsheet, which are automatically updated when a query or its results change.
  * [**Importing existing CSVs & XLSX files**](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/spreadsheet-tabs#importing-existing-csvs-and-xlsx-files) - Recreate existing formatting and formulas in Omni
  * [**Manually entering data**](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/spreadsheet-tabs#manually-entering-data)

Omni recommends connecting workbook queries as data sources whenever possible. This ensures that your data is current and, if needed, accessible outside of the spreadsheet tab.
###
[​](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/spreadsheet-tabs#connecting-workbook-queries)
Connecting workbook queries
The recommended way to add data to a spreadsheet tab is to connect an existing workbook query. This allows you to manipulate and format data while taking advantage of your existing data model. Open the spreadsheet’s settings by clicking the **drawer icon** (highlighted in the following image) in the left navigation: ![](https://mintcdn.com/omni-e7402367/pDLnBWL9E88CrUiD/images/docs/querying-and-sql/workbook/assets/images/spreadsheet-settings-7290476b32f7f36cf992af64d14e9bc1.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=pDLnBWL9E88CrUiD&q=85&s=2b66a4a92926b2d62ca682c03d892305) When a workbook query is added to a spreadsheet, Omni will add a **protected sheet** with the same name as the query to the spreadsheet. Data in sheets associated with workbook queries will automatically update when the query’s results or structure changes. For example, if you add a new column to a query, the associated sheet will also be updated to include the new column.
###
[​](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/spreadsheet-tabs#importing-existing-csvs-and-xlsx-files)
Importing existing CSVs and XLSX files
Data added using this method only lives in the spreadsheet tab where you upload it. If you need to use CSV or XLSX data outside of a spreadsheet tab, consider using [data input tables instead](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/data-input-csvs).
Omni also supports importing existing CSV and XLSX files into spreadsheet tabs! For XLSX files, Omni will preserve your formatting, formulas, and references, allowing you to recreate existing workflows and wire them up to live data. CSVs will be parsed into columns.
  1. In a workbook, create a new spreadsheet tab or add a blank sheet to an existing spreadsheet tab.
  2. Drag the file into the blank sheet. A **Drag CSV or XLSX here** message should display.
  3. Drop (release) the file to begin the import.

After the upload completes, you can edit the spreadsheet like you usually would.
Get started quickly by importing an [an Excel template](https://create.microsoft.com/en-us/excel-templates) - you can then customize it using your own Omni data.
###
[​](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/spreadsheet-tabs#manually-entering-data)
Manually entering data
To manually enter data, click into a cell and type or paste the data. **Note** : Data added using this method only lives in the spreadsheet tab you enter it into. It will not be accessible outside of the spreadsheet tab.
##
[​](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/spreadsheet-tabs#referencing-query-data)
Referencing query data
Data in other sheets in a spreadsheet tab can be referenced just like you would in Excel. This includes direct references like `'<SHEET_NAME>'!A1` or as arguments in [formulas](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/spreadsheet-tabs#creating-formulas).
###
[​](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/spreadsheet-tabs#creating-formulas)
Creating formulas
The formulas described in this section are **not** the same as Omni’s [table calculations](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/calculations). Spreadsheet tabs support additional formulas, and the syntax between Omni table calculations and spreadsheet tab formulas may differ slightly.
Formulas in Omni spreadsheets generally mirror those in Excel. To view all supported formulas, click the **Formulas** tab in a spreadsheet and then **Insert Function** : ![](https://mintcdn.com/omni-e7402367/pDLnBWL9E88CrUiD/images/docs/querying-and-sql/workbook/assets/images/spreadsheet-insert-function-eed81ec7e25add085482c861c01d0790.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=pDLnBWL9E88CrUiD&q=85&s=990f132af9397ccf8e8c87f4a078330d) Refer to the [Excel documentation](https://support.microsoft.com/en-us/office/excel-functions-by-category-5f91f4e9-7b42-46d2-9bd1-63f26a86c0eb) for detailed information about these formulas. If you prefer a more guided experience when using functions, select a function in this window and click **OK**. You’ll be prompted to fill in the formula’s arguments. You can also directly add formulas to sheets. In a cell or the formula editor, enter `=` to start building the formula. For example:
Copy
Ask AI
```
=AVG(A:A)

```

###
[​](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/spreadsheet-tabs#copying-with-references)
Copying with references
Omni supports copying a sheet connected to a workbook query to a new, editable sheet in a spreadsheet tab. Right-click on the protected query sheet and select **Copy with references** : ![](https://mintcdn.com/omni-e7402367/pDLnBWL9E88CrUiD/images/docs/querying-and-sql/workbook/assets/images/spreadsheet-copy-references-c15a4131bf96d29144710fcec27a22b1.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=pDLnBWL9E88CrUiD&q=85&s=35d4cbe2d1bfc317ab3007b97b0ae113) A copy of the results sheet will be created. Unlike the original protected sheet, you can directly edit the contents of the copied sheet: ![](https://mintcdn.com/omni-e7402367/pDLnBWL9E88CrUiD/images/docs/querying-and-sql/workbook/assets/images/spreadsheet-copied-result-tab-d3c7a3ddbce600593c8f227cd84b5eaf.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=pDLnBWL9E88CrUiD&q=85&s=a7a9bc3757fd96eda54234bc064dae87) **Note** : The new sheet uses absolute references to pull in data. This means that if the query’s results set changes, the data in the copied sheet will also change. Refer to the [Handling query changes section](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/spreadsheet-tabs#handling-query-changes) for more information and examples.
###
[​](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/spreadsheet-tabs#unlocking-spreadsheets-for-dashboard-editing)
Unlocking spreadsheets for dashboard editing
By default, spreadsheets on dashboards are read-only. If you want dashboard viewers to be able to edit cells - for example, to perform what-if analysis - you can unlock a spreadsheet tab. When a spreadsheet is unlocked and viewed on a dashboard, viewers can edit all cells in the spreadsheet. To unlock a spreadsheet:
  1. Open the spreadsheet’s settings by clicking the **drawer icon** in the left navigation.
  2. Toggle **Unlock spreadsheet** to **on**.


Unlocking a spreadsheet only affects how it behaves on a dashboard. In the workbook editor, all cells remain fully editable regardless of the toggle state.
###
[​](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/spreadsheet-tabs#handling-query-changes)
Handling query changes
When a workbook query is updated, the sheet associated with it in a spreadsheet tab will also be updated to reflect the changes. This includes - but isn’t limited to - structural changes like adding columns, changing a filter value, or adding pivots. Omni spreadsheets differ from Excel in the way that underlying data changes are “absorbed.” For example, if you have a hardcoded reference for columns `A:D` and a new column (`E`) is added, only the query sheet will be updated to include the new column. The sheet containing the reference will have to be manually updated to `A:E`. Let’s take a look at another example, this time with a query that uses pivots.
####
[​](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/spreadsheet-tabs#1-workbook-query-with-filters-and-pivots)
1. Workbook query with filters and pivots
The image below displays the results of a query with two filters:
  * **Category** - Only include specified product categories
  * **Created At** - Only include records for the **past 3 complete years**

The results of the query have been pivoted so that the table has columns for the years `2022`, `2023`, and `2024`. ![Workbook query results table for a query that has two filters. Results show the total sales price for product categories, pivoted by year for 2022, 2023, and 2024](https://mintcdn.com/omni-e7402367/pDLnBWL9E88CrUiD/images/docs/querying-and-sql/workbook/assets/images/spreadsheet-query-pivot-199da522008f6a656f424d5c9455b384.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=pDLnBWL9E88CrUiD&q=85&s=1f380167bd2ced34ca2a0e53e69064fe)
####
[​](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/spreadsheet-tabs#2-query-results-sheet)
2. Query results sheet
This image displays the sheet in a spreadsheet tab associated with the **Sale Prices by Year** workbook query. Notice that the years are in the `B`, `C`, and `D` columns, which matches the results table in the actual workbook tab. ![](https://mintcdn.com/omni-e7402367/pDLnBWL9E88CrUiD/images/docs/querying-and-sql/workbook/assets/images/spreadsheets-query-sheet-efd68d78d7a2c383c8b044b2591d1758.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=pDLnBWL9E88CrUiD&q=85&s=196c40f9ea03bd4c99d47fcb0e0270fe)
####
[​](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/spreadsheet-tabs#3-reference-query-results-data)
3. Reference query results data
This image displays a formatted sheet that references cells in the `Sale Prices by Year` sheet. Just like in the query results, this sheet contains a column for each year (or pivot). For example, data for `2022` is pulled from the `B` column in the `Sale Prices by Year` sheet. ![](https://mintcdn.com/omni-e7402367/pDLnBWL9E88CrUiD/images/docs/querying-and-sql/workbook/assets/images/spreadsheet-formatted-pivot-bc83616da3b6c23be5d3ade1816db7f5.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=pDLnBWL9E88CrUiD&q=85&s=fdd2323c4ae0c70a66ccfcf84a2be850)
####
[​](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/spreadsheet-tabs#4-change-filter-in-workbook-query)
4. Change filter in workbook query
Let’s look at what happens to a sheet when the underlying structure of the query results changes. In this example, the **Created At** filter has been changed to include only the **past 2 complete years** , resulting in the `2022` column being removed from the query results. ![](https://mintcdn.com/omni-e7402367/pDLnBWL9E88CrUiD/images/docs/querying-and-sql/workbook/assets/images/spreadsheet-query-pivot-2-d1e397736c16d841641d6f0e671b98a0.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=pDLnBWL9E88CrUiD&q=85&s=14dce0f1e1135484778f442e425759ad)
####
[​](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/spreadsheet-tabs#5-updated-query-results-sheet)
5. Updated query results sheet
When query results change, the sheet associated with the query will automatically be updated. This image shows the updated `Sale Prices by Year` sheet in the spreadsheet tab. Notice that it now only contains columns for `2023` and `2024`, which matches the results in the actual workbook tab. ![](https://mintcdn.com/omni-e7402367/pDLnBWL9E88CrUiD/images/docs/querying-and-sql/workbook/assets/images/spreadsheets-query-sheet-2-a734c15be9e20446d03fed2b2d5baa5b.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=pDLnBWL9E88CrUiD&q=85&s=e645320cbc64f9e0aa98eba08ae803ad)
####
[​](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/spreadsheet-tabs#6-impact-on-query-data-references)
6. Impact on query data references
In this last image, you can see what happened to the formatted sheet when the query results sheet it references changed. The references and formulas in the highlighted column are now incorrect. When the query’s filter included **the past 3 complete years** , the `D` column in the `Sale Prices by Year` sheet was populated. Because it was changed to **the past 2 complete years** , a column was removed and the data shifted to the left, leaving the `D` column empty. ![](https://mintcdn.com/omni-e7402367/pDLnBWL9E88CrUiD/images/docs/querying-and-sql/workbook/assets/images/spreadsheet-formatted-incorrect-pivot-453b5ca37466eb0a942c7d0fddc73023.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=pDLnBWL9E88CrUiD&q=85&s=abcc2df04aad4284c9e7c09956dcd33f)
###
[​](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/spreadsheet-tabs#removing-query-data)
Removing query data
You can remove workbook queries from a spreadsheet by unchecking them in the spreadsheet’s settings panel. **Note** : When a workbook query is removed from a spreadsheet, the sheet referencing the query will also be removed. This doesn’t delete the query from the workbook.
##
[​](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/spreadsheet-tabs#saving-your-work)
Saving your work
Changes in spreadsheet tabs aren’t autosaved. Periodically save your work by clicking **Save Sheet** in the spreadsheet’s **Home** tab: ![](https://mintcdn.com/omni-e7402367/pDLnBWL9E88CrUiD/images/docs/querying-and-sql/workbook/assets/images/spreadsheet-save-sheet-6be138f12dfbfab584e459cf65a4be4c.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=pDLnBWL9E88CrUiD&q=85&s=850a150497ff8fbddf202444fdfb1274) This button will be highlighted in blue when there are unsaved changes. Additionally, Omni will prompt you if you attempt to navigate away from the spreadsheet with unsaved changes.
##
[​](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/spreadsheet-tabs#displaying-spreadsheets-on-dashboards)
Displaying spreadsheets on dashboards
Spreadsheets on dashboards are read-only by default. To allow dashboard viewers to edit cells, [unlock the spreadsheet](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/spreadsheet-tabs#unlocking-spreadsheets-for-dashboard-editing) in the workbook editor. To edit the full spreadsheet, click **File > Edit** or the **Edit** button to open a draft of the document.
Spreadsheets can be included on a dashboard just like any other visualization. By default, Omni will only display the **first sheet** in the spreadsheet on the dashboard.
###
[​](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/spreadsheet-tabs#including-all-sheets)
Including all sheets
To display all sheets on a dashboard, first open the spreadsheet’s settings by clicking the **drawer icon** in the workbook’s left navigation panel. Then in the **Dashboard settings** section, toggle **Show tab strip** to **on** : ![](https://mintcdn.com/omni-e7402367/pDLnBWL9E88CrUiD/images/docs/querying-and-sql/workbook/assets/images/spreadsheet-show-tab-strip-210cf497ad45d7c47cd2e55ed91f7d59.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=pDLnBWL9E88CrUiD&q=85&s=5ff044893b901847dfe820c5d48dd231) When enabled, all sheets will display as tabs on the dashboard: ![](https://mintcdn.com/omni-e7402367/pDLnBWL9E88CrUiD/images/docs/querying-and-sql/workbook/assets/images/spreadsheet-all-tabs-dashboard-a6fb2cc421daf567225dd115f278ad1a.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=pDLnBWL9E88CrUiD&q=85&s=c0fba304d69401c0de784ee4659f1cc5)
###
[​](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/spreadsheet-tabs#changing-sheet-display-order)
Changing sheet display order
By default, Omni will display the first sheet in a spreadsheet tab when a dashboard is viewed. You can change the sheet order by dragging sheets in the spreadsheet tab in the workbook. When finished, click [**Home tab > Save Sheet**](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/spreadsheet-tabs#saving-your-work) to ensure the changes are reflected on the dashboard.
###
[​](https://docs.omni.co/analyze-explore/spreadsheet-tabs#exporting-spreadsheets)
Exporting spreadsheets
Spreadsheets can also be exported back to Excel. On a dashboard, hover over the right corner of a spreadsheet tile and click the ⠇ (three dots). Then select **Download XLSX**.

Getting started
# Onboarding to Omni as a Viewer
Intended for viewers, this six-part video series will help you get started with viewing dashboard content in Omni.
To follow the steps in this guide, you’ll need:
  * An Omni account
  * [Viewer](https://docs.omni.co/administration/users/permissions) permissions


1
[](https://docs.omni.co/getting-started/viewers)
Navigate the Omni platform
Learn how to [navigate the Omni platform](https://docs.omni.co/content/navigate), including how to browse content, apply themes, and add content to your favorites.
2
[](https://docs.omni.co/getting-started/viewers)
Understand permissions
What can you do in Omni as a Viewer? Learn about Omni’s [connection](https://docs.omni.co/connect-data/setup) and [content permissions](https://docs.omni.co/share#content-access-permissions), how to share pre-built dashboards, and how to update dashboard permissions.
3
[](https://docs.omni.co/getting-started/viewers)
Discover what can be built in Omni
See what can be built in Omni, with the goal of inspiring requests made of your builder teammates.
4
[](https://docs.omni.co/getting-started/viewers)
Troubleshoot 'Can't display chart' errors
There may be times when you run into `Can't display chart` errors when viewing a dashboard. Learn what’s happening and how to resolve it using Omni’s [AccessBoost feature](https://docs.omni.co/share#boosting-permissions-with-accessboost).
5
[](https://docs.omni.co/getting-started/viewers)
Filter on dashboards
Filtering allows you to focus only on the data you care about. Learn about the power and flexibility of Omni dashboard filters.
6
[](https://docs.omni.co/getting-started/viewers)
Deliver and download results
While Omni supports [downloading results](https://docs.omni.co/visualize-present/dashboards/download) on a one-off basis, [deliveries and alerts](https://docs.omni.co/share/deliveries) allow you to define where and when you want your data. In this video, you’ll learn about your options for downloading results and how to set up Omni deliveries and alerts.
